<Resp>None</Resp>< name>
Toan Duong< /name>
< review>
Upfront notice: this is not my usual balanced review. You can get the ambience, service, and other factors from the numerous reviews on here. My five stars rating is solely for the uniqueness of the OLD CALIFORNIA TACO (OCT) here. I have not seen it anywhere else. It was tasty. It exists only here. It deserves  five stars for being.

$7.99 for a taco? Si senior. It's the size of a dinner plate and it was worth it. This behemoth size puts many burritos to shame. And I finished it in one seating. And I hated myself for finishing it.... but that's beside the point. Let's get back to the OTC

It's a cross over between a taco and a flauta. The shell is a large fluffy fried tortilla folded in half. Inside is filled to the brim with a layer of beans and your choice of meat. Mine was asada and it was very very good. The toppings of salad, sour cream, cheese, tomato, and salsa were then layered on top of the taco and filled out the plate. It was an impressive and intimidating sight for a taco. It was served with knife and fork. And you need them. There was no way to eat this beast with hands.

I imagined two amigos seating at a camp fire on the range somewhere in CA reminiscing of home made tacos from the old country. They talked with gusto and bravado...

Jose: the tacos here just ain't right
Roberto: they are so leeeeto here I'm still hungry.
J: my home town taco was bee-g and proper
R: I bet mine was bee-ger.
J: You should see my HT taco. It's bee-ger than your hand.
R: My HT taco is bee-ger than two hands.
J: Well my HT taco is bee-ger than a dinner plate.....

Thus began the legend of the OCT< /review>
</record>
</dataset><record>

< text>
I'm a filmmaker and I love The Prospect Studios (also known as ABC Television Center, a lot containing several television studios located at 4151 Prospect Avenue in the Los Feliz neighborhood of Los Angeles, at the corner of Prospect and Talmadge Street (named in honor of silent screen star Norma Talmadge), just east of Hollywood. I work here on General Hospital and I enjoy it. For more than 50 years, this facility served as the West Coast headquarters of the American Broadcasting Company before the network moved its main headquarters to the Walt Disney Studios in Burbank, California. From 1949 to 1999, ABC-owned Los Angeles television station KABC-TV was also located there. Truly inspirational. The station moved to a new state-of-the-art facility located on a portion of Disney's Grand Central Creative Campus (GC3) in nearby Glendale, California, in December 1999. The Walt Disney Company, which acquired ABC in 1996, continues to own and operate the facility to this day. I'm looking forward visiting again. Best, George Anton ANTFLIX< /text>

< Review>
Prospect Studios is a bad neighbor. Year after year they have failed to do anything about the filth, street trash and debris that collects in front of the studio grounds.

The build up of trash and leaves causes the gutters to block up and flooding to occur during our rainy season.

The sidewalks bordering the studio are essentially their front yard and as such are Prospect Studios responsibility. How Prospect Studios can live with their clients driving through such a mess is beyond me.<//Review>

< Review>
What sets this place apart from every other bike shop is the affable nature of each and every person you meet here. I know other riders out there know what I'm talking about when you go into a bike service shop and they make you feel like you are just lucky to be there.
Not here. You get a name and a handshake from each person you meet, the mechanics are knowledgable and dont give you grief if your a noob.

The prices are fair and the work is done without excess services being pushed. I cannot say how highly I reccomend these people and their business.<//Review>

<userid>104745565929433688409< /userid>< Text>
This place has its act together.  No wait staff robots here.  Exhibition cooking exposing the full kitchen with seating all around.  It's a joy to watch this group in action.

We were right opposite the handmade pizza production. Station 1, sprinkling the paddles with coarsely ground corn, air stretching the road-dimple-sized dough portions to fit the paddle, ladeling a 1 inch wide thin layer of olive oil around the outer region 1" from the edge; then station 2 starting from the inside edge of the olive oil ladeling their tomato sauce to look like the Target logo. Soft Mozzarella cheese chunks are then dropped to for the sauce circles.  Off to station 3 for toppings and then into the oven.  Beautiful to watch the artistry and obvious caring and dedication.

This routine never let up during our 45 minutes.  Yes we had a pizza, mushrooms and fresh arugala.   You will enjoy anything you order.</Text>

I would add this place to the list of my favorite Italian restaurants in LA! Cozy and pretty. Service was outstanding and excellent - I felt really welcomed by the staff when I was there.

Their lunch menu was simple but sincere. We had their Tagliarini and Margherita. The noodles were special and we loved them. Sitting at the bar, we saw the whole process of making and baking the pizza, which was then served directly from the kitchen to our table, and the pizza was just of the kind that would bring one joy.

In addition to all the afore-mentioned, their passionfruit meringue tart stunned me. A symphony of the cloud-like meringue topping, the sour curd, and the crispy buttery pastry - it was more delicious than impressive looking!<//text>

5</rate>
<Text>This place has its act together.  No wait staff robots here.  Exhibition cooking exposing the full kitchen with seating all around.  It's a joy to watch this group in action.

We were right opposite the handmade pizza production. Station 1, sprinkling the paddles with coarsely ground corn, air stretching the road-dimple-sized dough portions to fit the paddle, ladeling a 1 inch wide thin layer of olive oil around the outer region 1" from the edge; then station 2 starting from the inside edge of the olive oil ladeling their tomato sauce to look like the Target logo. Soft Mozzarella cheese chunks are then dropped to for the sauce circles.  Off to station 3 for toppings and then into the oven.  Beautiful to watch the artistry and obvious caring and dedication.

This routine never let up during our 45 minutes.  Yes we had a pizza, mushrooms and fresh arugala.   You will enjoy anything you order.<//Text>< pictures>

< review>
Ordered the pork belly sausage and kale pizza. We asked our server to have the kale removed, so it was just a pork belly sausage pizza. It was delicious. The tomato sauce was creamy delicious and the sausage was also very tasty. It was a very thin 12" pizza that required folding lengthwise to eat without flopping over. Nothing wrong with that, just trying to give an accurate description. The crust was crunchy and gooey; almost Neapolitan. One pizza should be enough to for an average couple. We also ordered the steak salad...also, delicious. The beef was a bit livery, but tasty. The avocado, tomatoes, and mixed greens were flavorful and had a tasty vinaigrette. The wait staff was helpful and friendly and would acknowledged if they didn't know the answer to something and would get an answer right away. The restaurant is a bit loud and a bit cramped, but it's to be expected for this type of restaurant. We went on a Thursday at about 2pm and it was full, but a couple tables were available. With a glass of wine the total was about $64. I would recommend this place for a casual meal for 1-2 people. They probably can accommodate more people, but given the size and popularity, larger parties should probably call ahead.<//review>

< review>
Don't wear your Yeezy's here! Unfortunately my first impression left me with a bad taste in my mouth. The waiting area for a table is quite narrow, it's also the walkway in and out of the restaurant. Low and behold, a 400lb dude stepped on my foot, and it actually hurt, a lot. So ladies, be careful if you're in heels.

Regarding the food, it was actually really good, but you have to order correctly. The garlic knot was really good, but if you let it sit for more than 5 minutes, the bread really soaks up the half-cup of oil that the bread is just sitting in, and caution for the string, it's obviously there and not edible, but it somehow ended up in my mouth. I would recommend the garlic knot.

The mixed mushroom pizza was amazing, so was the pasta and the chicken meatballs, as well as the pound cake dessert.

Staff was amazing, employees were super friendly towards each other, friendly to us, and very helpful in describing what each dish consisted of.

In conclusion, watch out for people stepping on your feet, and order cautiously.<//review>

<Review>Milo and Olive is a cute little italian place tucked away on a busy street in Santa Monica - I love the open atmosphere and bustling vibe of the restaurant. It is on the small side, so waiting for a table for a group larger than 3 can be a pain but the staff are extremely nice, accommodating and try to make it as painless as possible. This can definitely be avoided if you don't go during peak hours.

<name>YJ W<//name><Date>1397277019505<//Date>< rate>

< review>
I love all things bakery, and I have to say Milo and Olive is like the perfect restaurant for me: there are pizzas, pastas, baked goods, beer, and they're open late! The pizzas are delicious (albeit a tad too greasy), the garlic knot is a flavorful, bready mess, and you can use the remaining garlic as a spread or in other dishes--totally worth it! Definitely try their salads if you visit, both that I've tried were delicious, and even the vegetarian pasta special we tried was amazing. <Date>1525895083992<//Date>< Rating>

< review>
Came here on a Thursday night and it was already super packed by around 7:30. There was about a 45 minute wait, but we left our name and moved in towards the back of the restaurant where there was some room to stand and ordered a bottle of wine while we waited. They were super attentive to us while we waited, and even let us order our food while we were still standing in order to have it ready once we sat down because we were in a bit of a rush.

Regarding drinks, we did a bottle of wine even though some of us wouldn't have preferred it, because the cocktails were on the expensive side. I'm from NYC, but $15 for a cocktail with dinner was still a lot, considering with 2 of those you're already at a $30 tab each not including food, tax, tip, etc. The wine was luckily great though, so we were fine with it once we tried it.

The ambiance was super upbeat while still being cozy. The place itself is small and while it was a bit loud (it was super crowded), it still had an intimate feel. The staff was all extremely friendly and accommodating - my friend who we were with is vegan and found limited options on the menu, but they answered all her questions and were able to switch a few things around to make some of the menu items vegan for her.

She ended up getting the gnocchi and my friend and I split the margarita pizza. Both were really good, but also pretty pricey for what it was.

We really liked Milo and Olive, but I wouldn't recommend it for a casual dinner - better for something a little more formal or special just cased on the price! Definitely a lot of menu options I would have liked to try, but the pricing in general dissuaded me from adding sides, apps etc.

Also, wanted to note that they let us (and everyone) know that "A 3% charge is added by the restaurant to all checks to help offer fully covered healthcare to our employees." While I think this is awesome, I don't necessarily think that's what customers should be paying for? Not sure how it works in other restaurants, but I know plenty of servers and bartenders that get full benefits without it being added to customers' bills. Maybe it's worked into the prices in other ways, but I can tell you for sure if the prices had been any higher we would have relocated for what was a casual night out!</review>
